## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a concentration A(t), which is the standard setup for chemical kinetics modeled by ordinary differential equations. With only t and A available, plausible structures are mass-action rate laws (functions of A) and possibly explicitly time-dependent rate coefficients (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion, e.g., surface-limited or saturated regime)
- First-order decay (mass-action): dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive-like kinetics, simple relaxation)
- Pseudo-first-order with source term: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A (net production/decay with constant inflow/outflow approximation)
- Second-order (bimolecular/self-reaction): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (A + A -> products, or effective second-order loss)
- General nth-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical/global reaction order)
- Offset equilibrium relaxation: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (first-order approach to equilibrium concentration c1)
- Reversible-like linear kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 (forward loss balanced by constant reverse/source over a regime)
- Autocatalytic / self-accelerating then limited: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product-catalyzed growth with depletion/limitation without explicit logistic form)
- Self-inhibition (crowding/complexation) rational law: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 * A + 1) (effective rate reduced at high A)
- Substrate inhibition-like loss: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 * A**2 + 1) (stronger high-concentration suppression)
- Time-dependent first-order (linearly changing rate constant): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (temperature/condition drift approximated as linear in time)
- Time-dependent first-order (exponentially changing rate constant): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (ramping conditions, activation by external program)
- Empirical time forcing plus decay: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) + c3 * A (external feed/drive plus linear kinetics)
- Mixed-order (parallel pathways): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous unimolecular and bimolecular loss channels)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Mass-action dominance → dA_dt primarily a function of A with negative sign; monotone depletion often fits -c0*A or -c0*A**c1
- Reaction order identification → log(-dA_dt) vs log(A) approximately linear suggests dA_dt = -c0*A**c1
- Approach to equilibrium → sign change around A ≈ c1 indicates relaxation form dA_dt = -c0*(A - c1)
- Parallel pathways → curvature that cannot be fit by a single power law often indicates sums like -c0*A - c1*A**2
- High-concentration slowdown → rates that grow sublinearly with A suggest rational inhibition forms like -c0*A/(c1*A+1)
- Self-acceleration then slowdown → dA_dt increasing with A at low A but decreasing at high A suggests autocatalytic-limited form c0*A*(c1-A)
- Time-varying conditions → systematic residual drift vs t at fixed A suggests k(t) multiplying A, e.g., dA_dt = -k(t)*A with k(t)=c0+c1*t or c0*exp(c1*t)
- Physical non-negativity constraints → models should typically keep A(t) ≥ 0; overly large positive dA_dt at small A is often unphysical unless there is a source term
- Initial transient vs long-time tail → a fast early drop followed by slower decay can indicate mixed-order terms or inhibition (e.g., -c0*A - c1*A**2 or rational forms)
